Simon interprets this to mean that we say the first limb was from a defective animal and the rest therefore are proper sacrifices.</i>, all that is defective was in his hand, so he says here all that is impure is in his hand. Rebbi Zeїra asked, may we not say that Rebbi Eliezer said it only because of a fence<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">He disagrees with R. Simon; his position is that of R. Eleazar in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 77b" href="/Zevachim.77b">Babli (<i>Zebaḥim</i> 77b</a>) that R. Eliezer permits the limbs on the altar only if at least two of the same kind are brought simultaneously, so that one of them at least is valid. The “fence” is the fence around the law, a measure of precaution that no biblical law could possibly be violated; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Demai 1:2:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Demai.1.2.4"><i>Demay</i> Chapter 1, Note 89</a>.</i>? Does not Rebbi Eliezer agree that for a <i>seah</i> lifted from <i>ṭevel</i> he must give a name to its tithes<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 6:2" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).6.2">Tosephta 6:2</a>: “A <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into less than 100 and made it <i>dema‘</i>, if it was <i>ṭevel</i> he uses it as heave and tithes for other produce or he gives a name to the heave of the tithe.” 6:3: “A <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into 100 of Sabbatical produce shall be lifted, less than that must be left to rot.” <i>Ṭevel</i> is forbidden to everybody, including a Cohen, but the Cohen may turn it all into heave and heave of the tithe without actually separating anything.</i>? If you say the <i>seah</i> which fell is the <i>seah</i> which came up, it would not be necessary to give a name to its tithes<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">If it were 100% heave, no tithes would be possible.</i>! Rebbi Mana said, Rebbi Zeїra is correct since we have stated after this<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 3. If R. Eliezer would consider all that came into his hand as heave, it would be pure and would not have to be eaten with the precautions indicated in the Mishnah.</i>: “A <i>seah</i> of pure heave which fell into a hundred of impure profane produce,” and Rebbi Eliezer does not disagree! The colleagues argued before Rebbi Yose: Rebbi Simon is correct, because otherwise would one burn heave because of a “fence”? He said to them, are the six doubts which we have stated not because of their “fences”? Do we not also burn here because of its “fence”<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">The reference is to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tahorot 4:5" href="/Mishnah_Tahorot.4.5">Mishnah <i>Ṭahorot</i> 4:5</a>: “For six doubts one burns heave: For the doubt of field of pieces (a field where a grave was ploughed), the doubt of earth from a Gentile country (which is impure by tradition), the doubt of the garments of a vulgar person (who does not observe the rules of purity), the doubt of found vessels, the doubts of spittle and urine (from unknown persons), if one certainly touched them but does not know about their status of purity one burns heave. R. Yose says, even on a doubt whether one touched them in a private domain (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 3:1:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.3.1.2">Chapter 3, Note 10</a>), but the Sages say, on that doubt in a private domain one suspends and on a public road it is pure.” The normal procedure for heave that may be impure is to “suspend”, i. e., to leave the heave to rot and then dispose of it if it is no longer food. The questioner assumes that all questionable heave is suspended; R. Yose points out that there are instances in which questionable heave is burned.</i>? The colleagues said, we asked before Rebbi Yose: In any case, if it is impure heave, it should be burned, if it is profane, why could it not become impure<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">Why do the Sages have to oppose R. Eliezer; could the lifted <i>seah</i> not be burned and all problems would be eliminated?</i>? He said to us, is it not eaten as heave? Heave cannot be eaten except if it is pure, maybe impure? Do you not agree that if a doubt of impurity arose in its place that he cannot burn it<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">The position of the Sages in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tahorot 4:5" href="/Mishnah_Tahorot.4.5">Mishnah <i>Ṭahorot</i> 4:5</a>: If the heave was of doubtful status before it fell into the 100 other <i>seah</i> (“in its place” before it fell), it would have to be suspended, not burned. Why could its replacement be burned now?</i>? What is the difference whether a doubt of impurity arose at another place or at its place? But if you want to question, then question what Rebbi Hoshaiah stated, since Rebbi Hoshaiah stated: “A <i>seah</i> of pure heave that fell into 100 <i>seah</i> of impure heave<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">There is no Tosephta dealing with this case, but everybody agrees that all must be burned; one does not lift one <i>seah</i> to let it rot.</i>.”
Crackers are about half of a <i>seah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Either this is a scribal error for “half an egg”, cf. the end of Mishnah 1, or the translation of ניקודין is not “crackers” but “totally dry” following <a class="refLink" data-ref="Rashi on Bekhorot 22b" href="/Rashi_on_Bekhorot.22b">Rashi (<i>Bekhorot</i> 22b</a>) who translates the verse <a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 9:12" href="/Joshua.9.12"><i>Jos</i>. 9:12</a> הנה יבש והיה נקדים “behold, it is dry and was totally dry” and comments on our Mishnah: “Now, even though there is purity and impurity, the pure part will not become impure without preparation; the impure part becomes voided in the plurality and should be eaten ניקודים.”</i>.
Ḥizqiah said, even the profane food there should be eaten only as dry crackers because of their <i>ḥallah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">The heave from the dough which has to be eaten by a Cohen in purity under the rules of heave, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:20" href="/Numbers.15.20"><i>Num</i>. 15:20</a>.</i>. His word says that the prohibition of the outsider becomes insignificant but the prohibition of impurity does not become insignificant<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">If he is worried about heave, there are two prohibitions to be observed: No outsider (one who is not a Cohen) may eat from it and it may not be eaten in impurity. Since he does not require that all should be given to the Cohen as <i>dema‘</i>, it follows that the prohibition of the outsider has disappeared. Since he is worried about impure heave, the prohibition of impurity has not disappeared. The argument cannot refer to the Mishnah here, since everything is impure and any <i>ḥallah</i> must be burned. Therefore, Ḥizqiah must refer to Mishnah 2, one <i>seah</i> of impure heave which is in 100 <i>seah</i> of pure profane grain.</i>. The arguments of Ḥizqiah seem inverted. There<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">This seems to refer to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Challah (Lieberman) 2:5" href="/Tosefta_Challah_(Lieberman).2.5">Tosephta <i>Ḥallah</i> 2:5</a>: “Impure flour which was mixed with pure flour but the impure is less than its measure (less than the volume of an egg), if he takes [<i>ḥallah</i>] he says: This should be <i>ḥallah</i> except for the impure part in it.” He cannot declare all of it as <i>ḥallah</i> since it might contain impure flour and impure <i>ḥallah</i> is forbidden as food. But the part of impure flour in the dough is certainly less than the volume of an egg and, therefore, all of it may be eaten by a Cohen. {The explanation of this and the next paragraph follows R. H. Kanievski.}</i>, he says: How much can be in a dough that he should be able to make it in purity<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">How much impure flour can be in the dough so that pure <i>ḥallah</i> can be taken?</i>? Ḥizqiah said one sixth of four <i>qab</i> in four <i>qab</i><sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">If will be seen in the next paragraph that <sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup>/<sub>6</sub> <i>qab</i> is much more than the volume of an egg, Ḥizqiah holds that, in this case, one may separate a small cake for <i>ḥallah</i> (whose normal size should be 1/24 of the entire dough) to be sure that it does not contain the volume of an egg of impure dough and turn it into <i>ḥallah</i>. The remainder may then be worked in impurity. Since <i>ḥallah</i> follows the rules of heave, it must be taken from the dough itself. Ḥizqiah must follow R. Eliezer who in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Challah 2:2:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Challah.2.2.1">Mishnah <i>Ḥallah</i> 2:4</a> permits to give one <i>ḥallah</i> for all breads in one large basket. If the bread destined for <i>ḥallah</i> is separated from the large impure breads by small loaves of volume less than one egg, no contamination can take place. (The basis of this device is <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Challah 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Challah.2.3.1">Mishnah <i>Ḥallah</i> 2:7</a>).</i>. And here he says so<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">He rejects the trick which he recommends for <i>ḥallah</i> and requires that all be consumed either dry or kneaded with pure fruit juice.</i>! Rebbi Yose said, there, when he kneaded the dough and then separated, but here when he separated and then kneaded<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">“There” is here, in <i>Terumot</i>, when it is his intention of processing all flour together; “here” is there, in <i>Ḥallah</i>, when he is prepared to separate a small cake to be kneaded in purity, the rest in impurity.</i>.
Rebbi Abbahu said, all our days we were groping about this as with a blind man’s stick until we learned it from mathematical computation. How much is in a <i>qab</i>? 24 eggs<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">This is standard; a <i>qab</i> is 6 <i>log</i> and a <i>log</i> 4 eggs. The same division is accepted in the Babli.</i>. How much is in a <i>seah</i>? 96 eggs<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">This is nonstandard; the <i>seah</i> in all other places is 6 <i>qab</i>, here it is 4. The <i>seah</i> here must be the Roman <i>modius</i> which is 16 <i>sextarii</i>, and the <i>sextarius</i> is the <i>log</i> since <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Kelim 17:11" href="/Mishnah_Kelim.17.11">Mishnah <i>Kelim</i> 17:11</a> identifies the רביעית, the fourth part of the <i>log</i>, with the Roman <i>quartarius</i>, the fourth part of the <i>sextarius</i>. {In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 83a" href="/Eruvin.83a">Babli <i>Erubin</i> 83a</a>, a <i>modius</i> is estimated as the volume of 217 eggs. Current practice follows the Yerushalmi here.} The amount of pure <i>ḥallah</i> to be given from 96 eggs would be the volume of 4 eggs. But since the verse (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 15:21" href="/Numbers.15.21"><i>Num</i>. 15:21</a>) reads: “<i>From</i> the beginning of your dough you shall give …” the dough made for <i>ḥallah</i> cannot be exactly the volume of four eggs since something profane must be left over.</i>. One sixth of it are 16 eggs. If he makes a dough of six, it contains an impure egg<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">It is assumed that the flour was thoroughly mixed and homogenized. Since 6 = 96/16, a dough in the volume of 6 eggs contains exactly 1 egg of impure flour and is impure.</i>. If he makes from four, nothing is left. What does he do? He makes a dough from five and takes four.
The statement of Ḥizqiah says, on condition that no impurity the volume of an egg touch the indentation<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">The meaning of this word depends on the interpretation of Mishnah <i>Ṭahorot</i> 1:10: “Loaves of sacrificial bread which have water in their גוּמוֹת, if one of them became impure by a crawling thing, they all are impure; for [loaves of] heave they make impure two stages and disqualify a third. If there is damp fluid between them, even for heave all is impure.” According to Maimonides, the indentations are depressions in the bread that still contain fluid. (It seems that for this reason, he wrote in the first version of his Commentary: “Indentations left on top of the bread at the time of cooking”, which in the last version he changed into: “at the time of baking.”) According to R. Simson, followed by R. Asher ben Ieḥiel, the baking sheet has depressions into which the dough is placed to obtain loaves of uniform size. The explanation of R. Simson seems to be required by the formulation in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Tahorot 1:5" href="/Tosefta_Tahorot.1.5">Tosephta <i>Ṭahorot</i> 1:6</a>: “Loaves of sacrificial bread <i>in their</i> גוּמוֹת.”</i>. A statement of Rebbi Joḥanan says, on condition that no impurity the volume of an egg touch the dough<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">The dough for the profane loaves.</i>. Rebbi Yose said to Rebbi Jeremiah: Is it not reasonable that Ḥizqiah spoke to the past and Rebbi Joḥanan spoke to the future<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Ḥizqiah has two restrictions compared to R. Joḥanan. First, all that is in contact with any fluid he declares impure where R. Joḥanan strictly insists that only the volume of at least one egg may induce impurity. Second, in case of doubt he extends impurity retroactively to all food in contact with the questionable dough; R. Joḥanan rejects retroactivity.</i>? He said, that is my opinion also. What is an indentation in the opinion of Rebbi Joḥanan<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Under which circumstances does he admit that the situation envisaged by Ḥizqiah leads to impurity?</i>? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Jonah: Explain it that he made a dough with one in seventeen and it came to a dough of two <i>seah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">This criticism is levelled at Ḥizqiah himself and at R. Abbahu’s interpretation of his position. The interpretation is rejected because it presupposes that pure and impure flour can be completely mixed, with a constant percentage of impure flour in the pure. Since presumably the two kinds are indistinguishable to the eye, mixing can not be assumed to be perfect. As a rough estimate, R. Joḥanan will admit R. Abbahu’s solution if not more than the volume of 17 eggs are mixed with 2 <i>seah</i> of pure flour (somewhat below 9%) and thoroughly mixed.</i>.
Rebbi Abba bar Mamai asked: Does this not contradict Rebbi Yose bar Ḥanina? As Rebbi Yose bar Ḥanina said, a carcass<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">A dead animal not ritually slaughtered.</i> can become insignificant in slaughtered<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Slaughtered by cutting its throat; cf. Arabic سحط “to cut somebody’s throat.” The biblical Hebrew שחט has exactly the same meaning.</i> [meat]; it becomes insignificant for touch, but for motion it cannot become insignificant<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Carcasses transmit impurity in the first degree by touch (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 11:27" href="/Leviticus.11.27"><i>Lev</i>. 11:27</a>), and original impurity if they are carried (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 11:28" href="/Leviticus.11.28"><i>Lev</i>. 11:28</a>) even if never touched. If a piece of carcass meat is mixed up with pieces of slaughtered meat, probably it touched a piece belonging to the pure majority, but when all are carried, certainly the carcass piece also was carried. Since the impurity by touch is only probable, it can be disregarded under certain conditions. The impurity by carrying is certain and can never be disregarded.</i> for slaughtered [meat] can never become carcass [meat]<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">This argument is ascribed to Rav Ḥisda in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Beitzah 38b" href="/Beitzah.38b">Babli (<i>Beẓah</i> 38b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 23a" href="/Menachot.23a"><i>Menaḥot</i> 23a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bekhorot 23a" href="/Bekhorot.23a"><i>Bekhorot</i> 23a</a>), as a general principle to R. Ḥanina, the father of R. Yose ben R. Ḥanina. The Babli concludes that slaughtered meat cannot become insignificant in carcass meat because it is possible for carcass meat to acquire the purity of slaughtered meat by rotting and becoming unusable as food while it is impossible for slaughtered meat to acquire the impurity of carcass meat.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, there it is impossible for slaughtered [meat] to become carcass [meat], but here profane produce may become heave<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">While profane produce may never be used to give heave, if a layman ate heave, he has to replace it by an equal amount of profane food (plus a 25% fine) which acquires the sanctity of heave, cf. Mishnah 6:1.</i>. Rebbi Ḥizqiah said, Rebbi Simon raised the question and Rebbi Abba bar Mamai explained it.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 6:1" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).6.1">Tosephta 6:1</a>.</i>: “A <i>seah</i> of heave that fell into less than a hundred makes it <i>dema‘</i>. One does not pay for it the amount and a fifth for another place nor from another place for this except by computation60.” This is for substances which cannot be mixed. But for substances which can be mixed one goes after the plurality. If most of it is heave, it is heave, if most is profane, it is profane<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">As far as payment goes; the argument does not apply to fixing the <i>dema‘</i>.</i>.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> One <i>seah</i> of impure heave which fell into 100 <i>seah</i> of pure heave, the House of Shammai forbid<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">They forbid the entire heave as inpure (even if completely dry).</i> and the House of Hillel permit. The House of Hillel said to the House of Shammai: Since pure it is forbidden to outsiders and impure is forbidden to priests<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">Outsiders and Cohanim.</i>; just as pure [heave] can be lifted, so impure should be lifted. The House of Shammai answered them no, if simple profane produce which is permitted to outsiders lets pure [heave] be lifted, can one infer that heave, operating under stringent rules, may let the impure be lifted? After they conceded, Rebbi Eliezer said it should be lifted and burned but the Sages say, it was lost in its minority<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Since everything is heave, all the 101 <i>seah</i> may be eaten by a Cohen as pure heave.</i>.<br>One <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into one hundred<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">100 <i>seah</i> of profane produce.</i>, was taken out, and fell into another place: Rebbi Eliezer says it creates <i>dema‘</i> like certain heave but the Sages say, it creates heave only in proportion<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">The amount of certain heave in what was lifted is only 1/101 of the lifted produce; in order to remove <i>dema‘</i> one needs only 1 <i>seah</i> of profane produce.</i>.<br>One <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into less than one hundred and made it <i>dema‘</i> and from the <i>dema‘</i> fell into another place; Rebbi Eliezer says it creates <i>dema‘</i> like certain heave but the Sages say, <i>dema‘</i> creates heave only in proportion; sour agent makes sour only in proportion<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">Sour dough of heave which was added to dough to make it rise turns the entire dough into heave (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Orlah 2:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Orlah.2.3.1">Mishnah <i>Orlah</i> 2:6</a>). If from the dough anything was taken for another batch of dough, the latter becomes heave only if the proportional part of the original souring agent alone would have been enough to make the new dough rise. The three cases “in proportion” mentioned here are repeated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Temurah 1:4" href="/Mishnah_Temurah.1.4">Mishnah <i>Temurah</i> 1:4</a>.</i>, and drawn water invalidates a ritual bath only in proportion<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">If a <i>miqweh</i> contains a little less than the minimum 40 <i>seah</i> and three <i>log</i> of water are added from a vessel to bring it over the limit, the entire water becomes unfit for a ritual bath. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Temurah 12" href="/Temurah.12">Babli (<i>Temurah</i> 12a–b</a>) gives two explanations for the Mishnah here; there is no Yerushalmi on this part of the Mishnah. According to the final determination of the Babli, “in proportion” here has a meaning totally different from the two preceding cases, in that water from vessels invalidates only if the vessels are in proportion to the three <i>log</i>, i. e., if the water is added from at most three vessels, not from four or more. This is accepted by Maimonides in his Code (<i>Miqwaot</i> 5:1) with the concurrence of R. Abraham ben David (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosafot on Temurah 12b:4:1" href="/Tosafot_on_Temurah.12b.4.1"><i>Tosaphot Temurah</i> 12b, <i>s. v.</i> יוסף</a>).</i>.<br>One <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into one hundred<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">100 <i>seah</i> of profane produce.</i>, was taken out, and another one fell in: the latter is permitted until there will be more heave than profane<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">The process of lifting can be repeated until one would have more heave than profane produce if each time only profane matter would have been taken out and all heave stayed in. In that case, the mixture will be forbidden by biblical law as soon as there is not more profane than heave matter. The Tanna of the Mishnah assumes that it is impossible that in all these processes only heave be lifted; even in the worst case some profane grain will be lifted. Therefore, he does not have to say “permitted as long as the volume of heave is less than that of profane grain.” The grain is permitted unless the amount of heave which fell in is larger than half the original amount of profane grain. This is the position of R. Simson and R. Abraham ben David.<br>Maimonides’s explanation is difficult to understand. He permits the mixture if at most 100 times 1 <i>seah</i> fell into the produce and was lifted. He gives no explanation. R. Joseph Caro explains that in the previous Mishnaiot, when the Sages assert that the heave counted in the remaining produce is computed proportionally, they assume that there was perfect mixing of heave and profane before the excess <i>seah</i> was lifted. But in that case, if <i>t</i><sub>i</sub>, <i>h</i><sub>i</sub> are the amounts of heave and profane in the mixture after <i>i seah</i> fell in and were lifted,<br><i>h</i><sub>i</sub><i>=</i> 100(100/101)<sup>i</sup><br>and <i>h</i><sub>i</sub><i>&lt;</i> 50 for integer <i>i &gt;</i> 69. {The solution of 100(100/101)<sup>i</sup> = 50 is <i>i =</i>69.66 …} Since, by definition, <i>t</i><sub>i</sub> <i>+ h</i><sub>i</sub><i>=</i>100, by the explanation of R. Joseph Caro, the process can be repeated only 69 times and RR. Simson and Abraham ben David would agree.</i>.<br>A <i>seah</i> of heave fell into 100 [profane] and before he managed to lift it, another one fell in: that is forbidden but Rebbi Simeon permits it.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Yudan bar Pazi and Rebbi Ayvo bar Naggari<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">Galilean Amora of the early fourth generation, student of R. Ḥiyya bar Abba and R. La.</i> were sitting and saying: We did state “after they conceded”; who conceded to whom? The House of Shammai to the House of Hillel or the House of Hillel to the House of Shammai? They said, let us go out and study. The went out and heard Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Jehudah bar Ḥanina: We never find the House of Shammai conceding to the House of Hillel except in this matter. Rebbi Jonah in the name of Rebbi Abbai<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">His name appears only here, and nothing more is known about him.</i> understood it from the following<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Ṭevul Yom</i> 2:7. For most severe impurities it is not enough that the impure person immerse himself in water; after the immersion, as <i>ṭevul yom</i> “immersed during the day”, he is pure only for profane food. For heave, and certainly for sacrifices, he becomes pure only at sundown. If in the period between his immersion and sundown he touches heave, it becomes unusable; this is classified as “impure in the third degree”. If the <i>ṭevul yom</i> touches a stream of heave fluid (wine or oil) poured from one vessel to the other, in the opinion of the Sadducees the entire fluid in both vessels becomes unusable (MMT lines 55–58). In rabbinic tradition, only the part touched by the <i>ṭevul yom</i> becomes unusable; the fluid cannot be used because unusable heave is contained in it, but it can be repaired by the usual lifting of one out of 101.</i>: “If someone pours from vessel to vessel and a <i>ṭevul yom</i> touches it, it should be lifted by 101.” If you say that the House of Hillel conceded to the House of Shammai that it cannot be lifted, who is the Tanna here, neither the House of Shammai nor the House of Hillel! Rebbi Ḥanina the son of Rebbi Hillel said, we might say that the House of Hillel stated that before they conceded. Rebbi Yose said, the Mishnah said so: “After they conceded, Rebbi Eliezer said it should be lifted and burned”, and is Rebbi Eliezer not a follower of Shammai? Rebbi Ḥinena said, the Mishnah said so, after they conceded one to another, the House of Shammai recused themselves and the others<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">The Sages, who always represent the tradition of the House of Hillel.</i> teach us. Rebbi Abin says, there is another answer<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">Which the House of Hillel could have given to the House of Shammai, in addition to the argument presented in the Mishnah.</i>, following what Rebbi Hoshaia stated: Since pure [heave], which for outsiders is forbidden as deadly sin, can be lifted, certainly also impure [heave] which is [prohibited] as positive commandment<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">Which is classified as a misdemeanor, rather than a felony.</i> for Cohanim.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, a <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into 100 of profane produce, anything will make it become insignificant<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">If one <i>seah</i> was lifted after a <i>seah</i> of heave fell into 100 profane <i>seah</i>, the new <i>seah</i> is only heave by rabbinic decree superimposed on a rabbinic obligation; it is heave in name only and can be made insignificant in the slightest amount of additional profane produce. Quoted in this sense in Halakhah 9:6.</i>. Our Mishnah disagrees with Rebbi Joḥanan: “It creates heave only in proportion<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">According to the Mishnah, the amount into which if fell must still be 100/101 times the amount lifted.</i>”. Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, Rebbi Joḥanan stated only: “It does not create any <i>dema‘</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">He had another version of the Mishnah before him.</i>” But<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">The Sages of the Mishnah speak of the case that the amount lifted was taken from the place the heave fell in, when one may assume that more genuine heave than profane grain was lifted. Rebbi Joḥanan speaks of the case when everything was well mixed; in Halakhah 9:6 this is expressed by: “he mills [the grain] and thereby permits it.”</i> they said only when there was more heave than profane, and he when there was more profane than the proportion of heave so that it should become insignificant in the plurality. Rebbi Eleazar said, only<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah which relates the disagreement of R. Eliezer and the Sages. Do the Sages permit the profane part of the <i>seah</i> that fell into <i>dema‘</i> to be added to the profane part of the <i>dema‘</i> to provide the necessary 100÷1 ratio?</i> if it fell into a <i>dema‘</i>. In the opinion of Rebbi Eleazar, are the lower and upper profane produce united to lift? Rebbi Eleazar wants to say that the lower profane produce becomes inert<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">The position tentatively ascribed to R. Eleazar in the previous sentence is that of R. Joḥanan. R. Eleazar is restrictive and requires the lifted heave to be neutralized on its own when it fell into <i>dema‘</i>, irrespective of the amount of profane produce in the <i>dema‘</i> into which it fell. This is the majority position in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 6:5" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).6.5">Tosephta 6:5</a>, opposed by R. Simeon and his son.</i>.
Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina said, only if it fell into five places, but if it fell into one place, even Rebbi Eliezer agrees. Rebbi Joḥanan said, even if all fell into one place, there is disagreement<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">In the opinion of R. Yose ben Ḥanina, R. Eliezer agrees in principle with the Sages that the heave in the lifted grain should be counted only in proportion but he thinks that if heave fell in several separate batches each batch needs separate 100-fold profane grain lifting whereas the Sages think that the heave is to be considered as evenly distributed through the entire <i>dema‘</i> grain. R. Joḥanan disagrees and holds that <i>dema‘</i> follows the rules of heave as far as consumption is concerned and, therefore, the lifted grain should be considered all heave.</i>. Ḥilfai said on that of Rebbi Eliezer, the lower profane produce becomes inert<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">R. Eliezer agrees in principle with the Sages that the heave in the lifted grain should be counted only in proportion but he holds that the heave part of the lifted grain is genuine heave with all its restrictions; the rest is just ballast and disregarded.</i>. But Rebbi Eleazar also said, the lower profane produce becomes inert. What is the difference between Rebbi Eliezer and the rabbis<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">If one combines Ḥilfai’s interpretation of R. Eliezer and R. Eleazar’s interpretation of the Sages, one fails to see the difference between them.</i>? Is one more restrictive with a lifted <i>seah</i> out of 100<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">R. Eliezer holds that the heave which fell is the heave which was lifted (cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 5:1:8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.5.1.8">Note 27</a>); he can state this only if he considers the remainder of the grain as inert.</i> or is one more lenient, following what Rebbi Joḥanan said, if a <i>seah</i> of heave fell into 100 of profane produce, anything will make it insignificant<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">For the Sages, this is also a position accepted by R. Eleazar, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 5:2:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.5.2.3">Note 82</a>. One sees that there is a big difference between R. Eliezer and the Sages, even if R. Eleazar accepts Ḥilfai’s argument.</i>?
It was stated: If the heave became a plurality it is as if he had added intentionally<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">It cannot be lifted even in very large amount of profane produce, as stated in Mishnah 9. If so much heave can fall into profane food it shows that the negligence borders on intentional misconduct.</i>. But did we not state<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Mikvaot 7:2" href="/Mishnah_Mikvaot.7.2">Mishnah <i>Miqwaot</i> 7:2</a>. The expression “he added” shows that a religious bath (<i>miqweh</i>) which contains the required amount (40 <i>seah</i>) of natural water, additional water may intentionally be added from vessels without impairing the validity of the bath.</i>: “If it contained 40 <i>seah</i>, he added a <i>seah</i> and removed a <i>seah</i>, it is in order.” How far? Rebbi Assi in the name of Rebbi Mana bar Tanḥum<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">An Amora in Tyre between the second and third generation of Galilean authorities.</i>, Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, up to the larger part of the <i>miqweh</i><sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 82b" href="/Yevamot.82b">Babli (<i>Yebamot</i> 82b</a>), it is made clear that in a <i>miqweh</i> of exactly 40 <i>seah</i>, exactly 20 <i>seah</i> can be added and removed. This also seems to be the meaning here.</i>. And here you say so? There it was a plurality, you add to it and it is in order. But here, every single <i>seah</i> needs 100 <i>seah</i>. Rebbi Yose said, this means that anything becoming insignificant by biblical law is activated by its own kind to become forbidden<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">Since 40 <i>seah</i> in a <i>miqweh</i> permit the addition of water from a vessel, once the water enters the <i>miqweh</i> its quality as poured from a vessel becomes insignificant and it becomes like natural (spring or rain) water. But if the added and removed quantities become more than 20 <i>seah</i>, the <i>miqweh</i> becomes forbidden. This proves that the insignificance of the invalid water is conditional. The principle stated here is accepted in both Talmudim.</i>.
Rebbi Simeon says, knowledge of it sanctifies; but the rabbis say, its lifting sanctifies it<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">Since 40 <i>seah</i> in a <i>miqweh</i> permit the addition of water from a vessel, once the water enters the <i>miqweh</i> its quality as poured from a vessel becomes insignificant and it becomes like natural (spring or rain) water. But if the added and removed quantities become more than 20 <i>seah</i>, the <i>miqweh</i> becomes forbidden. This proves that the insignificance of the invalid water is conditional. The principle stated here is accepted in both Talmudim.</i>.
It was stated: One <i>seah</i> of heave<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">This must be impure heave, as shown by the sequel.</i> that fell into one hundred, he says to the Cohen, am I not obligated to you for the value of firewood? Take the value of the firewood<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">It seems, as noted by R. Moses Margalit, that the impure heave was the property of a Cohen when it accidentally fell into less than 100 units heave. (It cannot be exactly 100 units as in the <i>baraita</i>, since then the heave would have to be lifted and eaten dry, as stated before.) Since impure heave is only usable as fuel, it may be sold to a Cohen as fuel.</i>! But he answers him, does a <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into less than 100 not make the entire heave <i>dema‘</i>? Does firewood create <i>dema‘</i>? Does he not in the end have to give it to another Cohen<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">Since nothing else can be done with impure <i>dema‘</i>.</i> who will pay him for the value of the fuel? How is that? He gives him the value of the fuel and they should split the rest<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">The rest over and above the one <i>seah</i>, which the owner may give to any Cohen of his choice for payment of its value as fuel.</i>. A person spilled barley into wheat. The case came before Rebbi Jehudah bar Shalom<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">An Amora of the fifth generation, mostly quoted in aggadic matters.</i> who said, let him pay the price of barley; they should split the rest<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">Here the situation is different; this really belongs to tractate <i>Baba Qamma</i> since the damage is visible. If A hurts B by pouring some of his barley into B’s wheat, A has to pay B the difference between the going rates for wheat and barley for B’s grain. If later somehow the rate for barley should rise, the profit has to be split between them since A and B are now joint owners of the grain.</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> A <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into 100, if he milled it and it lost volume, in proportion to what the profane lost, the heave lost, and it is permitted<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">One <i>seah</i> may be lifted and the rest is permitted. In this case, differences in quality between heave and profane grain are disregarded.</i>. A <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into less than 100, if he milled it and it increased in volume, in proportion to the increase of the profane is the increase of heave, and it is forbidden. If it is known that the profane wheat was of better quality<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">Yielding more flour and less bran.</i> than the heave, it might be permitted. If a <i>seah</i> of heave fell into less than 100 and more profane fell into it later, if it was in error, it is permitted, if intentional, it is forbidden<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">It is dema‘.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">The entire paragraph is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Nazir 6:8:2-4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Nazir.6.8.2-4"><i>Nazir</i> 6:10</a> (fol. 55c), part of it in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Orlah 1:3:6-17" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Orlah.1.3.6-17"><i>Orlah</i> 1:4</a> (fol. 61b).</i> Not only if the heave lost volume but even if only the profane grain lost but the heave remains as it was, he mills and permits. It was stated: “The waste of heave does not combine with heave to forbid the profane, but the waste of profane combines with the profane to lift the heave<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">If after milling, the heave without its waste would be 1/100 of the milled profane grain plus its waste, heave could be lifted.</i>.” Rebbi Vivian asked: Does the waste of heave combine with profane to lift the heave? Since Rav Huna said, the husks of what is forbidden combine to permit<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">The statement of R. Huna refers to <i>orlah</i>, fruits in the first three years of a tree’s life, which are forbidden for any use and, if they disappear among other fruits, in general make everything forbidden for any use unless the permitted part are 200 times more than the forbidden. Rab Huna instructs to count in the 200 all husks, both from profane as from <i>orlah</i> fruit.</i>, that means waste of heave combines with profane to lift the heave<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">If after milling, the heave without its waste would be 1% of the remainder, heave can be lifted.</i>. Rav Huna said, the shells of what is forbidden lift what is permitted. A <i>seah</i> of heave which fell into 100, one does not remove <i>zewanin</i><sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kilayim 1:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kilayim.1.1.1"><i>Kilaim</i> 1:1, Note 1</a>.</i> in it, into less than 100, one does remove the <i>zewanin</i> in it. Similarly, if one <i>log</i> of clear wine<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Of heave.</i> fell into 100 <i>log</i> of cloudy wine, one would not remove the latter’s dregs; if one <i>log</i> of cloudy wine fell into 100 <i>log</i> of clear wine, one would remove the former’s dregs.
It was stated: “One may mill from the start to permit<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">If one has <i>dema‘</i> and after milling, following the rule of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 5:3:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.5.3.2">Note 106</a>, it would be possible to lift the heave, one tells the owner to go ahead and mill even though the Mishnah is formulated only as a statement after the fact, if the owner milled it and now comes to ask a rabbinic authority on how to proceed.</i>.” The <i>baraita</i> is Rebbi Yose’s, since “Rebbi Yose said, one may collect to lift one in two hundred”<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Orlah 1:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Orlah.1.4.1">Mishnah <i>Orlah</i> 1:6</a>. Since this is a minority opinion, it cannot be practice to be followed.</i>. Rebbi Zeїra said<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Orlah 1:4:2-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Orlah.1.4.2-7"><i>Orlah</i> 1:5</a>, the statement is more complete: “R. Zeїra said, it is the opinion of everybody since Cohanim are used to mill <i>dema‘</i> in their houses.” Since this is a required process, one cannot object to its use.</i>, Cohanim are used to mill <i>dema‘</i> in their houses. What is the difference between them? <i>Kilaim</i> in a vineyard. In the opinion of Rebbi Yose, one mills to permit; in the opinion of the rabbis, one may not mill to permit.
Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: All forbidden things<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">Which can become insignificant in an appropriate plurality (60, 100, 200 times, as the case may be).</i>, if one added against them in error, it is permitted, intentionally it is forbidden. Is that not the Mishnah: “if it was in error, it is permitted, if intentional, it is forbidden”? The Mishnah is about heave, he comes to tell you about all other things.
Rebbi Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: Just as one has a duty to instruct about actions that should be done, so one has a duty to instruct about actions that should not be done. Rebbi Eleazar said, just as it is forbidden to declare the impure as pure, so it is forbidden to declare the pure as impure. Rebbi Abba bar Jacob said in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: If a practical case comes before you and you do not know whether to suspend or to burn<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">In order Ṭahorot, the rule is that heave impure by biblical standards must be burned but heave only impure by rabbinic standards must be “suspended”, <i>viz</i>, one must leave it to rot until it is no longer food and, therefore, pure according to all standards.</i>, always try to burn rather than to suspend since there is nothing in the Torah more distinguished than burned bulls and burned rams, and they are burned<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 10:18" href="/Leviticus.10.18"><i>Lev</i>. 10:18</a> it is established as a general rule that any sacrifice whose blood was brought into the sanctuary, to be sprinkled either on the golden altar or before the ark, must be completely burned.</i>. Rebbi Yose wondered, is it possible to infer from something whose commandment is in this for something whose commandment is not so<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">The simile is not convincing; one should not rush to treat rabbinic impurity as biblical.</i>?

Chapter 6



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody eats heave in error, he pays principal and fifth<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:14" href="/Leviticus.22.14"><i>Lev</i>. 22:14</a>: “Anybody who ate sanctified food in error must add its fifth to it and give the holy food to the Cohen.” In the Yerushalmi (6:1) and the Sifra [<i>Wayyiqra pereq</i> 20(8); <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 21:1-24:23" href="/Leviticus.21.1-24.23"><i>Emor pereq</i> 6(4</a>)], its <i>fifth</i> is interpreted to mean that the addition must be one fifth of the restitution, or one fourth of the principal. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bava Metzia 54a" href="/Bava_Metzia.54a">Babli (<i>Baba Meẓi‘a</i> 54a</a>) this is the opinion of R. Oshaia, whereas R. Jonathan refers its <i>fifth</i> to the principal. The latter opinion is never found in the Yerushalmi. There will be a discussion in the Halakhah whether the expression “give the holy food to the Cohen” means that the designation as reparation makes holy or only its delivery.</i>; whether he eats, drinks, or anoints<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Since the food enters his body, whether through the mouth or through the skin.</i>, whether the heave be pure or impure, he pays. The fifth and the fifth of the fifths<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">If he dedicated the fifth and then inadvertently ate this fifth, since it had become heave as stated in the next sentence, it is subject to the rule of the fifth and he must restitute both the fifth and an additional fifth (1/16 of the original amount.)</i> he does not pay in heave but in totally profane food which is turned into heave. All payments become heave. Although the Cohen may want to forgive this, he has no right to forgive.<br>If an Israel woman ate heave and then was married to a Cohen, ate the heave before a Cohen had acquired it, she pays principal and fifth to herself<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">Heave is eaten not only by a Cohen but also by his family (wife, children, slaves.)</i>, but if she ate heave which a Cohen had acquired, she pays principal to its owner and the fifth to herself since they said, he who eats heave in error pays the principal to its owner and the fifth to a person of his choice.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “If somebody eats heave in error,” etc. It is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:14" href="/Leviticus.22.14"><i>Lev</i>. 22:14</a>): “Anybody who ate sanctified food in error must add its fifth.” That it and its fifth make five<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 6:1:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.6.1.1">Note 1</a>. It is clear that the main inference is from the word עליו not quoted here.</i>.
Did not Rabbi Abbahu say in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">This is the attribution in all parallels in the Yerushalmi: <i>Šabbat</i> 11:5 (13b), <i>Baba Qamma</i> 7:2 (5d). <i>Šebuot</i> 3:1 (34b), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 3:1:2-19" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.3.1.2-19"><i>Ketubot</i> 3:1</a> (27c), except <i>Terumot</i> 7:1 (44c) in the name of R. Simeon ben Laqish, and here in the Rome ms. which reads תני. The parallel discussion in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 69a" href="/Shabbat.69a">Babli is <i>Šabbat</i> 69a</a>.</i>: If he is in error about fat but intentional about a sacrifice, he can be warned, is whipped, and brings a sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Unintentional deadly sins are atoned for, in general, by sacrifices or, as in the case of heave, by specified payments. Intentional sins cannot simply be atoned for; the guilt is eliminated either by punishment through a criminal court or by Divine justice (assuming the intentional sinner does not sincerely repent, otherwise repentance and the Day of Atonement will induce Divine mercy to wipe the slate clean.)<br>As explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kilayim 8:1:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kilayim.8.1.4"><i>Kilaim</i> Chapter 8, Note 9</a>, a criminal court can impose biblical sanctions only if criminal intent is proven by two witnesses. This means that two witnesses testify that the alleged criminal was warned about the criminality of the act he seems intent to commit. The situation here is that the perpetrator knew that eating fat (those fatty parts of domesticated animals which in a sacrifice have to be burned on the altar) was forbidden but did not know what the punishment would be. In the Babli, R. Joḥanan holds that if he knew that eating fat was forbidden but not that it was a deadly sin he committed an intentional sin but an unintentional deadly sin, just as described here by R. Abbahu. If duly warned, he can be punished for eating fat as a misdemeanor but in addition he has to bring a sacrifice for the aspect of deadly sin of which he was oblivious, as asserted here also. R. Simeon ben Laqish does not permit a sacrifice unless the person was ignorant of the fact that the act was punishable.</i>. Say also here, if he has intention about heave but is inadvertent about the fifth, one should warn him and he should be whipped and bring a fifth<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Why is eating heave by an unauthorized person, which also is a deadly sin, not treated similarly, with the payment of the fifth being the equivalent of a sacrifice?</i>. Rebbi Zeїra said, it is a decision of the verse, “if somebody eats heave in error,” that all his eating should be in error<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">He must not have known at all that his eating was punishable.</i>. If he is intentional in doubt it is as if he is unintentional in his certainty<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">R. Zeїra admits only two cases, if he intended to eat but was not sure that he ate heave, or if he ate certain heave but was oblivious of this fact all the time he was eating.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, this means that if somebody forgot after he knew, he is guilty unintentionally<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">This is described as the quintessential unintentional sin; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:4" href="/Leviticus.5.4"><i>Lev</i>. 5:4</a>: “Or a person who swears, by expression of his lips, to his advantage or detriment, about anything a person is apt to swear, <i>then he forgot</i>, but later remembered that he had incurred guilt about one of these.”</i>.
If somebody said, I would not touch the volume of an olive, but I will touch half the volume of an olive, Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya said, he is like a person who eats half the volume of an olive unintentionally and half the volume of an olive intentionally<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Everybody agrees that for any prohibition regarding solid foods, no punishment by an earthly court can be imposed if the quantity consumed was less than the volume of an olive. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 73b" href="/Yoma.73b">Babli <i>Yoma</i> 73b</a>, R. Simeon ben Laqish states that less than the established minimum in any case is not forbidden by the Torah, but R. Joḥanan holds that everything forbidden is forbidden in any quantity; it simply cannot be prosecuted if the quantity is minimal. In <i>Šabbat</i> 12:6 (13d), this position is ascribed to Rabban Gamliel and the question about two olive halves is not answered.</i>. Would Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya hold with Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish since Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, if he ate half the volume of an olive during one forgetting spell<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">As far as sacrifices in atonement of unintentional sins are concerned, acts committed during separate forgetting spells cannot be combined if half a measure is not sinful; cf. <i>Šabbat</i> 12:6 (13:d), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 105a" href="/Shabbat.105a">Babli <i>Šabbat</i> 105a</a>.</i>, he is free from punishment. So here, if he ate two times half the volume of an olive minus something, he is free from punishment. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish agrees in the case of prohibitions of usufruct<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">If <i>all</i> usufruct is forbidden, such as grain growing in a vineyard or food from an idolatrous sacrifice, half a measure must be forbidden because its use would be usufruct.</i>, Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish agrees in the case of the Day of Atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli, R. Simeon ben Laqish only holds that less than a measure, in that case less than the volume of an average dried fig, is forbidden by rabbinic decree. This contradicts the Yerushalmi since a rabbinic prohibition can never lead to an obligatory sacrifice.</i>, Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish agrees in case he would complete it in the future<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The forbidden material is activated by its own kind; cf. end of Halakhah 5:7.</i>.
Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is also in <i>Šabbat</i>14:4 (14d), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 8:3:2-15" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.8.3.2-15"><i>Yoma</i> 8:3</a> (45a); cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 80b-81a" href="/Yoma.80b-81a">Babli <i>Yoma</i> 80b–81a</a>. In the parallels, the statement about payment of principal only is asserted both for vinegar and a wheat grain.</i>: He who swallows heave vinegar is whipped<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">If he did it after due warning by two witnesses. The statement implies that drinking a fluid which most people do not use is still called drinking in the legal sense.</i>. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: He who chews a wheat grain of heave is whipped. It was stated: He who chews a wheat grain of heave pays the principal but not the fifth; Rebbi says, I am saying that he pays principal and fifth<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli, a parallel statement by R. Jeremiah in the name of R. Joḥanan speaks about chewing raw barley grains. This is considered a health hazard and therefore not included in the notion of eating in the sense of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:14" href="/Leviticus.22.14"><i>Lev</i>. 22:14</a>. Therefore, one has to pay for the value of what he took, as anybody must who took another’s property illegally, since even his own heave is not his property but a Cohen’s. The <i>baraita</i> here deals with raw wheat kernels which are not a health hazard; it is simply asserted that the fifth applies only to what is considered eating by a majority of the population.</i>. Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Ammi: The Sages agree with Rebbi about him who swallows heave vinegar after such <i>ṭevel</i>, that he pays principal and fifth because vinegar refreshes the spirit<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">If the person first drank <i>ṭevel</i> vinegar, which also is sinful but not subject to the fifth, and then added some more heave vinegar, that makes vinegar food as a folk medicine.</i>.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">The same statement also in Halakhah 7:1 (44c), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Ketubot 3:1:2-19" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Ketubot.3.1.2-19"><i>Ketubot</i> 3:1</a> (27b). In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yevamot 90a" href="/Yevamot.90a">Babli (<i>Yebamot</i> 90a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 54a" href="/Gittin.54a"><i>Giṭṭin</i> 54a</a>) the text is quoted in somewhat enlarged form but rejected (since impure heave is paid for as if it were fuel for principal and fifth, cf. Halakhah 5:8, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 7:2" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).7.2">Tosephta 7:2</a>) and reformulated to speak of pure heave; that changed text is in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 7:7" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).7.7">Tosephta 7:7</a>.</i>: If someone ate impure heave, he has to pay in pure profane food, but if he paid in impure profane, he discharged his obligation. Rebbi Nathan says, Symmachos says, if inadvertently, what he did is done, intentionally, he did not do anything<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">All traditions of Symmachos are R. Meïr’s. The invalidation of payment with impure produce is a fine imposed by the court. Since the Babli accepts R. Meïr’s decrees as a matter of principle, they have to reformulate the <i>baraita</i> as speaking of pure heave, inapplicable today. These decrees mostly are rejected as minority opinions in the Yerushalmi; there is no need for reformulation.</i>. There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 2:2.</i>: “One does not give heave from impure produce for pure.” It was stated in the name of Rebbi Yose<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 3:19" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).3.19">Tosephta 3:19</a>.</i>, “if he gave heave from impure produce for pure, whether inadvertently or intentionally, what he did is done.” It turns out that the single opinion<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">Symmachos (R. Meïr); the single opinion there is R. Yose. Since the subjects are different, there is no contradiction involved.</i> here is like the anonymous one there, and the single there like the anonymous here.
How is this<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Here starts the discussion of the Mishnah, that the replacement for heave and the fifth become subject to the laws of heave.</i>? Rebbi Zeïra in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: The replacements of heave are like heave in every respect except that what grows from them<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">If accidentally or inadvertently used as seeds.</i> is profane. The growth from heave is like profane in every respect<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">It is not subject to any purity requirements.</i> except that it is forbidden for outsiders. Rebbi Yose said, we have stated all three: The replacements of heave are like heave in every respect as we have stated, “he does not pay in heave but in totally profane food which is turned into heave.” Except that what grows from them is profane as we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 9:4: “The growth from heave is heave, the growth from the growth is profane.” It is clear from Mishnah 9:2 quoted next, that in most aspects, the growth from heave is like profane produce; it is like heave in that it is forbidden for non-Cohanim. Replacement for heave is not mentioned in that Mishnah.</i>, “the growth from heave,” which implies that what grows from replacement is profane. The growth from heave is like profane in all respects, as we have stated, “<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 9:2.</i> it is subject to gleanings, forgotten sheaves, and <i>peah</i>; Israel poor and Cohanim poor collect it,” except that it is forbidden to outsiders as we have stated, “Israel poor sell theirs to Cohanim for the price of heave but the money is theirs<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">In contrast to heave which is not the private property of the owner.</i>.”
It was stated: One does not use the complement of heave<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">As <i>Sefer Nir</i> notes, it is impossible that this <i>baraita</i> deal with replacement of heave in the sense of this Halakhah, since the Mishnah stated clearly that even “the fifth of the fifth” comes under the rules of heave. One has to assume, with R. M. Margalit, that one deals with the complement of heave, if the heave given turns out to be less than 1/60 of the harvest, and the farmer has to add the difference; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 8:2" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).8.2">Tosephta 8:2</a>. Since heave has no biblical minimum, that complement is only rabbinic heave and is not covered by <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:14" href="/Leviticus.22.14"><i>Lev</i>. 22:14</a>. But since the name of heave has been pronounced over it, it is not profane to be used for payment and cannot become <i>ḥallah</i>.</i> for payment of principal and fifth and for them one does not pay principal and fifth, it is not subject to <i>ḥallah</i>, and hands and the <i>ṭevul yom</i> do not make it unusable in the way they do not make profane unusable<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">The syntax of this sentence is garbled. The <i>ṭevul yom</i> makes heave unusable by his touch (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 5:2:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.5.2.2">Chapter 5, Note 68</a>), the same is true for unwashed hands which are always considered impure in the second degree. Profane food cannot become impure by touch of impurity of second degree in contrast to heave.<br>There is one opinion in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 5:2:2-11" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.5.2.2-11"><i>Soṭa</i> 5:2</a> (fol. 20a; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 18a" href="/Pesachim.18a">Babli Pesaḥim 18a</a>) that R. Aqiba asserts the possibility of third degree impurity for profane food, but it is clearly stated there that this is not acceptable practice.</i>. Even Rebbi Simeon and Rebbi Yose agree with this<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">It is not clear what the reference is. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Niddah 46b-47a" href="/Niddah.46b-47a">Babli <i>Niddah</i> 46b–47a</a>, R. Yose and R. Simeon free from <i>ḥallah</i> profane dough made to rise by heave (or <i>dema‘</i>) sour dough (since the action of the sour dough shows it is not insignificant even if less than 1% in volume). Similarly, in Mishnah <i>Ṭevul Yom</i> 3:4, R. Yose and R. Simeon declare that such a dough will become unusable by the touch of a <i>ṭevul yom</i>(and presumably also of unwashed hands). In both cases, the anonymous majority declares the dough to be profane.</i>.
“Although the Cohen may want to forgive this, he has no right to forgive.<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">Quote from the Mishnah.</i>” That is, if he did not yet separate. If he separated and after that ate<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">Not from the heave but the replacement of the heave.</i>, the disagreement of Rebbi and Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon, as it is stated: “(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:14" href="/Leviticus.22.14"><i>Lev</i>. 22:14</a>) ‘He shall give the holy food to the Cohen,’ his delivery sanctifies it so that he cannot eat it because it is heave. Also the separation sanctifies it so that he should be liable for principal and fifth, the words of Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon. Also the separation sanctifies it so that he should be liable for principal and fifth preventing him from eating it because it is heave.<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">The text is garbled in both mss.; the position of R. Eleazar is quoted twice, that of Rebbi is missing. It is probable that the original text was similar to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sifra, Emor, Chapter 6 7" href="/Sifra,_Emor,_Chapter_6.7"><i>Sifra Emor Pereq</i> 6(7</a>): “I could think that the separation [taking the payment out of some profane food] sanctifies it so that one would be obligated for principal and fifth; the verse says ‘He shall give the holy food to the Cohen,’ his delivery sanctifies it so that one [any non-Cohen] will be liable for principal and fifth, but the separation does not sanctify it so that he should be liable for principal and fifth, the words of Rebbi Meïr. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, also the separation sanctifies it so that he should be liable for principal and fifth.”</i>”
If he [the Cohen] forgave and after that he [the Israel owner] ate, there is disagreement between Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish since they disagreed: If he robbed heave from his maternal grandfather, a Cohen, Rebbi Joḥanan said, he has to pay to the tribe, but Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, he pays to himself<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">The robber has to repay the robbery, not double the value he took as is the rule for the thief. It is assumed that the grandfather died after he forgave the grandson for the robbery and the grandson is the only heir. According to R. Joḥanan, the grandfather could not forgive and the grandson cannot inherit; therefore, the restitution has to be made to a Cohen. According the R. Simeon ben Laqish, the grandfather can forgive and the grandson can pay the principal to himself as heir, then sell the heave to a Cohen and pocket the money.<br>The statement is also in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Pesachim 2:3:2-7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Pesachim.2.3.2-7"><i>Pesaḥim</i> 2:3</a> (29a).</i>. Rebbi Jonah said, Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish answered Rebbi Joḥanan thus: According to you, who says he has to pay to the tribe, did we not state: “If he stole heave of the Sanctuary, he has to pay two fifths and the principal<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 6:4. Stealing and robbing from the Sanctuary have the same status; there is no double restitution. A fifth is required for illicit use of heave (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:14" href="/Leviticus.22.14"><i>Lev</i>. 22:14</a>) and of property of the Sanctuary (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:16" href="/Leviticus.5.16"><i>Lev</i>. 5:16</a>). The two obligations are independent of one another and computed on the same basis.</i>.” Should he not pay three<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">This is only a potentiality, not a certainty. If he denied stealing under oath, another fifth is due (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:16" href="/Leviticus.5.16"><i>Lev.</i> 5:16</a>). The heave can become property of the Sanctuary only if the Cohen dedicated it. Therefore, if the Cohen may forgive repayment, the thief cannot be forced to swear and there never can be three fifths. But according to R. Joḥanan, the tribe should be able to force the thief to swear in court and the Tanna should have noticed the possibility of a third fifth.</i>? Rebbi Yasa in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: The Torah said, it takes him out of his robbery. Rebbi Zeïra said to Rebbi Ammi: Two things you say in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan but you do not say why. Rebbi Joḥanan said, it takes him out of his robbery but you do not say why. It is so, “he shall give the holy food to the Cohen;” once he gave it, it stopped being his robbery<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Since robbery and sanctity are incompatible, once it is holy it is not subject to the laws of robbery and the third fifth claimed by R. Simeon ben Laqish is not applicable.</i>. You say in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, at the place of its slaughter should be its burning<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">The red cow whose ashes cleanse from the impurity of the dead (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19" href="/Numbers.19"><i>Num</i>. 19</a>) must be slaughtered on the stake; its carcass cannot be moved.</i>. You do not say why. Rebbi Eleazar in the name of Rebbi Hoshaia, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 19:5" href="/Numbers.19.5"><i>Num</i>. 19:5</a>: “On its excrement shall be its burning.” How do you understand this? Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Ammi: At the place of its exit from life shall be its burning<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">The entire statement is R. Hoshaia’s in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Zevachim 113" href="/Zevachim.113">Babli <i>Zebaḥim</i> 113</a>, in opposition to R. Joḥanan who requires the carcass to be moved in case it was slaughtered at a place from which the Temple doors are not visible; cf. also <i>Sifry Ḥuqqat</i> 124.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan follows Rebbi<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the disagreement discussed in the previous paragraph. Since only handing the restitution to the Cohen turns it into heave, the Israel grandson of a Cohen cannot make restitution until he gives it to some Cohen.</i>, Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish follows Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Since separation already sanctifies, when the restitution was set apart before the death of the grandfather it is now legal heave in the hand of the Israel grandson.</i>. Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya said, even if Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish would hold with Rebbi, but only for something he is obligated to give to a Cohen; but for something he is not obligated to give to a Cohen<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">In our case, he inherits it legally from his Cohen grandfather.</i>, even Rebbi will agree since that is a Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Bekhorot</i> 1:6. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bekhorot 12b" href="/Bekhorot.12b">Babli (<i>Bekhorot</i> 12b</a>) holds that the rules for first-borns depend on special expressions in the appropriate verses and are not derived from general principles, against the Yerushalmi. (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 18:15" href="/Numbers.18.15"><i>Num</i>. 18:15</a>) “You should certainly redeem the human firstborn, and the firstborn of the impure animal you shall redeem.” For R. Eliezer, “certainly” refers to both cases, for the Sages only to the human firstborn. The redemption for a donkey is a lamb (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 13:13" href="/Exodus.13.13"><i>Ex</i>. 13:13</a>), for a human it is 5 <i>šeqel</i>(<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 3:47" href="/Numbers.3.47"><i>Num</i>. 3:47</a>).</i>: “If he separated the redemption of a first-born donkey and then it died, Rebbi Eliezer says one is responsible for alienation<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">If the lamb was designated for the redemption and then either stolen or lost, the owner must give another lamb as replacement. If the young donkey dies before the lamb is delivered, it is holy and must be buried but the lamb is not given to the Cohen.</i> as for the five tetradrachmas of the [human] first-born; but the Sages say, he is not responsible for alienation, as for Second Tithe.<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">If the lamb is lost, the owner has fulfilled his duty and the donkey is his. If the young donkey dies before the lamb is delivered, it is a profane carcass and the lamb must be delivered to the Cohen.</i>” Rebbi Eliezer will agree about first-born donkeys he inherited from the estate of his maternal grandfather, a Cohen, that he sanctified it when he separated it<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Cohen may give the lamb to himself; in that case, separation is all that is needed.</i>.
One who ate the heave of a Fellow has to pay the Fellow, one who ate the heave of a vulgar person has to pay the vulgar person<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">The notions of Fellow and vulgar person are explained in the Introduction to Demay. The vulgar person is unable to keep his food in purity; giving him pure food, as required by the Mishnah, would be forbidden waste.</i>. Does he then not deliver his pure food to a vulgar person? How does he do it, he gives both to a Cohen Fellow, takes the price of one of them and gives that to the vulgar Cohen<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">The amoraic text here has a parallel in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Terumot (Lieberman) 7:5" href="/Tosefta_Terumot_(Lieberman).7.5">Tosephta 7:5</a>: “He who eats heave of a vulgar [Cohen], pays principal and fifth to a Cohen Fellow; the Fellow takes money and indemnifies the vulgar [Cohen].</i>. Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya said before Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish, this follows him who says, its separation sanctifies. But for him who says, the delivery sanctifies, does it not need acquisition in any case<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">If there is no sanctification without delivery then there is no repayment without delivery and the Cohen Fellow should not be able to acquire heave that is not due him.</i>? He said to them, he operates through the services of a third person<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">The Cohen Fellow does not acquire the heave for himself but for the vulgar Cohen. He can do that since it is for the vulgar’s benefit. Then he has to buy the heave for himself from what he had acquired for the third person. Since this is a formal institution, the vulgar’s consent is implied.</i>.
If she did not manage to pay before she was divorced<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">If she has no children, she reverted to the status of Israel and is forbidden to eat heave.</i>? Come and see, if she had so many tithes, would they not be hers<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">If she got heave or Heave of the Tithe as a Cohen’s wife, it remains her property even if she cannot eat it now but must sell it to somebody who can.</i>? There tithes are defined but here the heave is still undefined<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Since she did not pay, the heave is not designated yet and undetermined things cannot be acquired.</i>. What compares to this? First-born of donkeys<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">It is difficult to know what is meant since there is no Yerushalmi to <i>Bekhorot</i>. It seems that one refers to the opinion of the Sages (Note 48) that the lamb is the Cohen’s property upon designation, before delivery. In this case, the heave would remain hers if designated before the divorce.</i>.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If one serves heave to his workers or his guests, he pays the principal and they pay the fifth<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">He pays the principal since he robbed the Cohen of his heave. They pay the fifth since they ate heave inadvertently and the fine of eating heave inadvertently is the payment of the fifth.</i>, the word of Rebbi Meïr. But the Sages say, they pay principal and fifth and he pays them the price of their meal<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">The Sages hold that the person who eats heave inadvertently has to pay principal and fifth. The host, in addition to the grave sin he incurred by leading innocent people into sin, is fined by having to pay his workers the price of their meal as if it had been profane food, while they pay only <sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup>/<sub>4</sub>of the price of heave, which probably is much less.</i>.<br>He who steals heave but does not eat it pays double restitution for the value of heave<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Since this is what he stole.</i>. If he ate it, he pays twice the principal and a fifth. The principal and the fifth from profane food<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">Restitution for the heave, following Mishnah 1.</i> and a principal the value of heave. If he stole heave of the Sanctuary and ate it, he pays two fifths and the principal<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 6:4. Stealing and robbing from the Sanctuary have the same status; there is no double restitution. A fifth is required for illicit use of heave (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 22:14" href="/Leviticus.22.14"><i>Lev</i>. 22:14</a>) and of property of the Sanctuary (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:16" href="/Leviticus.5.16"><i>Lev</i>. 5:16</a>). The two obligations are independent of one another and computed on the same basis.</i> since double restitution does not apply to the Sanctuary<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">The reason is given at the end of the Halakhah.</i>.<br>One does not pay with gleanings, forgotten sheaves, <i>peah</i>, and abandoned property<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">All these are exempt from heave; while they are permitted for profane use they are not profane since they are God’s gift to the poor.</i>, nor with First Tithe whose heave was taken, nor with Second Tithe<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">R. Meïr holds that Second Heave is Heaven’s property given to the farmer. Since it can never become heave, it is excluded as payment. The Sages consider Second Tithe and dedicated property after redemption, and First Tithe whose heave was taken, as totally profane since their sanctity has been transferred to the money of redemption.</i>, nor with dedicated food that was redeemed, for dedicated food cannot redeem dedicated food, the words of Rebbi Meïr. But the Sages permit the latter.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Now Rebbi Meïr says, they pay, and the Sages say, they pay, what is between them? Rebbi Joḥanan said, the meal itself is between them. Rebbi Meïr said, the meal is the resposibility of the employer, but the rabbis say, the meal is the resposibility of the workers<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">The responsibility vis-à-vis the Cohen is either on the person who actually ate the Cohen’s property or on the person who caused the trouble.</i>. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, the exertion is between them. Rebbi Meïr said, the exertion is the resposibility of the employer, but the rabbis say, the exertion is the resposibility of the workers<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Cohen is not compensated by money but by fully profane food, whose resposibility is it to procure the fully profane food in the correct amount?</i>. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish: To what can this be compared, to one who sells something to another person, but it turns out that it was not his [to sell]. Does he not have to replace his buy? If you hold with Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish, this is fine. But if you hold with Rebbi Joḥanan, who said, the meal itself is between them, and you say so? He said following Rebbi Meïr. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina: The value of the meal is between them. If he promised them to feed them profane honey-cakes but he fed them heave honey-cakes. Did they not eat already? This follows him who says, a person’s soul is afraid of <i>ṭevel</i><sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">The workers are overcompensated to account for the mental anguish caused them by their employer.</i>.
Rebbi Yannai said, the Mishnah is split<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">The entire argument refers only to the last case, heave stolen from the sanctuary.</i>. If there is the size of an olive but it is not worth a <i>peruṭah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">A <i>peruṭah</i>, a small Hasmonean coin, ⅙ or ⅛ of an as. Theft of less than a <i>peruṭah</i> is not prosecutable and does not entitle the injured person to ask for restitution.
